  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ba8f7d28-9977-4b9b-9c94-634098b610b6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_170764856" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170764856" />
    <a title="Diana • Book of Secrets" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3453249-diana-book-of-secrets"><img alt="Diana • Book of Secrets" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418921078p2/3453249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170764856?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana • Book of Secrets" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana • Book of Secrets" href="/user/show/3453249-diana-book-of-secrets">Diana • Book of Secrets</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3453249-diana-book-of-secrets?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170764856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13519202350123755604">Wildflower Hill is a poignant tale of two women living in different decades but whose lives are strongly intertwined. I dearly loved this book! The story of Beattie and her granddaughter Emma was completely absorbing. Beattie was a Scottish immigrant who moved to Tasmania, Australia, at the start of the Great Depression. Someone had told her once that "there are two types of women in the world...those who do things, and those who have things done to them." As a poor, unwed mother, she kept that </span>
  <span id="freeText13519202350123755604" style="display:none">Wildflower Hill is a poignant tale of two women living in different decades but whose lives are strongly intertwined. I dearly loved this book! The story of Beattie and her granddaughter Emma was completely absorbing. Beattie was a Scottish immigrant who moved to Tasmania, Australia, at the start of the Great Depression. Someone had told her once that "there are two types of women in the world...those who do things, and those who have things done to them." As a poor, unwed mother, she kept that thought in the forefront of her mind as she struggled against poverty and prejudice. Against insurmountable odds, she became the owner of a prosperous sheep farm in rural Tasmania, though it was not without great hardship and heartache.<br /><br />Set in 2009, Emma's story is effortlessly woven in with Beattie's. Emma is a prima ballerina in London. Proud of her success as a dancer, she didn't realize how it had totally consumed her life until a knee injury put an end to her career. Left with no other options, she returns home to Sydney. Emma is told that she has inherited a farm in Tasmania that her grandmother ran in the 1930s. Beattie had not been there for many years and used the place for storage, so Emma decides to head south to clean out the place in order to sell it. Upon arrival Emma finds boxes and boxes full of Beattie's old possessions, including letters, photos and business records. As Emma sorts through everything, she slowly uncovers family secrets buried for decades.<br /><br />I have not been moved by a book quite so much in a very long time. I really enjoyed the author's writing style, including the rich descriptions of the settings. It was easy to picture myself there too. Wildflower Hill stirred up many emotions for me - heartache, joy, anger, and frustration. Ultimately it is a very inspirational story about the power of perseverance and realizing what is truly important in life. Both Beattie and Emma were strong female characters written in a way that I felt like I was sharing their experiences with them. I loved how important parts of the story were told through old-fashioned letters. The last letter written by Beattie that Emma finds had me sobbing. The ending was bittersweet and very satisfying. I would highly recommend Wildflower Hill to fans of women's fiction. It is a story that will stay with me for a long time. ♥ <br /><br />Disclosure: I received a copy of this book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13519202350123755604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_192274891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192274891" />
    <a title="Stacie Vaughan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4778983-stacie-vaughan"><img alt="Stacie Vaughan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387074199p2/4778983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192274891?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacie Vaughan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacie Vaughan" href="/user/show/4778983-stacie-vaughan">Stacie Vaughan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780733623752" href="/book/show/9322690-wildflower-hill">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192274891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2875846119253464670">Wildflower Hill is at the top of my list for favourite books of the year and I would even say I consider it one of my favourite books of all time. It was absolutely wonderful. It's the kind of the book that leaves a lasting impression. I finished it a couple weeks ago and I am still thinking about it.<br/><br/>I think of one of the reasons why Wildflower Hill really touched me was the rich characters especially Beattie. I fell in love with her strength and kindness. I envied how she dealt so courageously </span>
  <span id="freeText2875846119253464670" style="display:none">Wildflower Hill is at the top of my list for favourite books of the year and I would even say I consider it one of my favourite books of all time. It was absolutely wonderful. It's the kind of the book that leaves a lasting impression. I finished it a couple weeks ago and I am still thinking about it.<br /><br />I think of one of the reasons why Wildflower Hill really touched me was the rich characters especially Beattie. I fell in love with her strength and kindness. I envied how she dealt so courageously with all the difficult situations life threw her in and she never once stopped to feel sorry for herself. This woman endured SO MUCH heartache that I was literally sobbing and even thinking back and imagining myself in the situation she was in, makes me misty eyed.<br /><br />This book brought out so many emotions in me and to me, that's a sign of a good book. I love books that can make me feel for the characters and be in the moment with them rather than just reading and observing. I felt anger towards Beattie's parents for abandoning her, and was furious with Beattie's "husband" and his wife. I don't want to give the story away so I want to be careful what I say.<br /><br />The story goes back and forth between the present day with Emma, the ballerina and back to the 1920s and 30s to her grandmother, Beattie's time. It's perfectly woven though so you don't feel like its jumping back and forth. I think Kimberley Freeman did an amazing job intertwining the two generations and developing the family history that becomes so important to Emma in the present day.<br /><br />I also really enjoyed the scenes in the Tasmanian countryside. Wildflower Hill appears to be a breathtaking location and I was taken away with all the vivid description of the countryside.<br /><br />This book is a "must-read". I'm going to read it again because I loved it that much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2875846119253464670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_232773674" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/232773674" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1632609-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307368032p2/1632609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232773674?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/1632609-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=dual-timeline">dual-timeline</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232773674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3609088657716049887"><b>Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>From the blurb and reviews, I though <i>Wildflower Hill</i> would be a proper dual-timeline story. You know the sort: someone discovers a letter or photo relating to an elderly relative which hints at a tantalising long-lost secret. The story then takes two paths: the quest for the truth in the present and the slow revelation of it in the past, with the two stories being poignantly entwined. I love books like this.<br/> <br/>However, this one actually reads far more like a rags-to-riches saga fu</span>
  <span id="freeText3609088657716049887" style="display:none"><b>Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br />From the blurb and reviews, I though <i>Wildflower Hill</i> would be a proper dual-timeline story. You know the sort: someone discovers a letter or photo relating to an elderly relative which hints at a tantalising long-lost secret. The story then takes two paths: the quest for the truth in the present and the slow revelation of it in the past, with the two stories being poignantly entwined. I love books like this.<br /> <br />However, this one actually reads far more like a rags-to-riches saga full of determination and heartbreak. This isn’t a bad thing, far from it; I also love sagas and quickly became engrossed in Beattie’s heart-wrenching tale of love and loss. The problem for me was that this saga kept being interrupted by a present-day story which had no bearing on the past, no place in the book. Yes, long-lost letters and photos were found, but this happened half way through, by which time the past was emotionally gripping and had no need for Emma’s present. It’s natural in a dual-timeline for the present to be the secondary story to the past, but they’re normally closely linked and have a poetic fluidity between them. I didn't feel any of that here.<br /><br />Beattie’s tale of passion and sacrifice broke my heart and made me cry. If this book had been a straightforward saga it would have been as easy 4 or 4.5 stars. Emma’s tale of self-absorbed whining bored me silly, so much so that I ended up skimming her sections; 1.5 stars at best. If only the two parts had a relevance, a connection, a poignancy. Or if only it has just been Beattie’s haunting story.... </span>
  <a data-text-id="3609088657716049887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226012357" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1659641822596638234">I picked up this book because it was supposed to be like a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/615274.Kate_Morton' title='Kate Morton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kate Morton</a> novel. I guess it sort of was, but not quite up to par. It had the same general plot set up as Morton's novels do: a young relative investigating/discovering family secrets alternated with the family in question's life. Even the time frame was the same: present day + world war era. Unfortunately, the similarities ended there as far as I was concerned. The historical pieces read like someone who did some research and lacked th</span>
  <span id="freeText1659641822596638234" style="display:none">I picked up this book because it was supposed to be like a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/615274.Kate_Morton" title="Kate Morton" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Morton</a> novel. I guess it sort of was, but not quite up to par. It had the same general plot set up as Morton's novels do: a young relative investigating/discovering family secrets alternated with the family in question's life. Even the time frame was the same: present day + world war era. Unfortunately, the similarities ended there as far as I was concerned. The historical pieces read like someone who did some research and lacked the genuineness that I've come to love with Morton's novels. There was little detail, and it just didn't manage to keep my attention. The first half of the book was significantly more bearable than the second half. Also, the book felt more like a chick lit novel than a Morton novel. Boring, predictable, and altogether generic. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1659641822596638234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9404005390808017150">This story wasn't as impressive as I had hoped it would be, but it was still good. It deals with family secrets which are slowly revealed to the reader as we follow two women from two different eras. Furthermore, one of them lives in Tasmania, Australia and the other one on the other side of the world, in London. <br/>I love stories that deal with people, relationships and multiple perspectives, however this one at times became too sweet and convenient for my taste. I think that if you've read a fair</span>
  <span id="freeText9404005390808017150" style="display:none">This story wasn't as impressive as I had hoped it would be, but it was still good. It deals with family secrets which are slowly revealed to the reader as we follow two women from two different eras. Furthermore, one of them lives in Tasmania, Australia and the other one on the other side of the world, in London. <br />I love stories that deal with people, relationships and multiple perspectives, however this one at times became too sweet and convenient for my taste. I think that if you've read a fair amount of books like these, this one won't surprise you a bit. You see where things are going, and in the end I was cringing my toes at all the morals that were put out in the open. <br />I still maintain that this was a good and entertaining story; it just didn't impress me in the way I was hoping for, but I'm still glad I read it and got the story behind Beattie and Emma. </span>

    <a title="Jenny Q" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2661064-jenny-q"><img alt="Jenny Q" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257813597p2/2661064.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2661064-jenny-q?shelf=my-favorite-reads">my-favorite-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168928732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13272023981858503991">This is a moving story of a woman's triumph over adversity, and the lessons she passes along to her granddaughter. Beattie Blaxland is an amazing character. When the story begins she's nineteen with dreams of becoming a fashion designer. Instead she ends up pregnant and homeless--but not defeated. She's smart, compassionate, hardworking, self-sacrificing, and she stands up for what she believes in. She's not perfect, but she's tough as nails and knows an opportunity when she sees one. She does w</span>
  <span id="freeText13272023981858503991" style="display:none">This is a moving story of a woman's triumph over adversity, and the lessons she passes along to her granddaughter. Beattie Blaxland is an amazing character. When the story begins she's nineteen with dreams of becoming a fashion designer. Instead she ends up pregnant and homeless--but not defeated. She's smart, compassionate, hardworking, self-sacrificing, and she stands up for what she believes in. She's not perfect, but she's tough as nails and knows an opportunity when she sees one. She does whatever it takes to provide for her daughter, tackling poverty and bigotry, and the conventions that have long held women back in small-town Australia during the depression and World War II.<br /><br />In the present day, Beattie's granddaughter Emma comes home to Australia after an exalted, whirlwind career as a prima ballerina ends abruptly due to an injury. Emma and Beattie are two very different women. Beattie's early life was one of struggle and uncertainty; Emma's was one of privilege and status. But Emma has to learn how to live without dancing and without a purpose, how to make friends, how to take care of herself. She's very surprised to discover that her grandmother left her an old farm estate, Wildflower Hill in Tasmania, and she goes there intending to prepare it for sale. But the house is full of boxes of Beattie's personal belongings--letters, photos, mementos--and as Emma goes through them she begins to discover who her grandmother really was and how much Wildflower Hill meant to her. Along the way she learns a lot about her own capabilities and what's truly important in life.<br /><br />I was utterly absorbed in this story from start to finish. The writing is lovely, the characterization is rich, the pacing is perfect, the narrative switches between Beattie in the past and Emma in the present in all the right places; I laughed, I cried, I got angry--and I never wanted it to end. But end it did, and it was one of the most satisfying, fitting, and perfect endings I've seen in a long time. Loved it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13272023981858503991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer55302473638295891">I didn't care for this book at all. The author did a poor job of making her story come to life. I just kept thinking to myself, "people don't act like this. People don't talk like this." Beatty was presented as though she were a victim of her society, but in actuality she was a victim of her own poor judgment and her inability to adapt to her circumstances. It was very hard to feel any sympathy for her.<br/><br/>Also, I was disappointed that I never felt a really strong sense of a time or place. At one po</span>
  <span id="freeText55302473638295891" style="display:none">I didn't care for this book at all. The author did a poor job of making her story come to life. I just kept thinking to myself, "people don't act like this. People don't talk like this." Beatty was presented as though she were a victim of her society, but in actuality she was a victim of her own poor judgment and her inability to adapt to her circumstances. It was very hard to feel any sympathy for her.<br /><br />Also, I was disappointed that I never felt a really strong sense of a time or place. At one point, kangaroos are mentioned and I wondered where kangaroos had come from, until I remembered the story was set in Australia. Freeman didn't do a good job of making me feel absorbed by the physical or cultural environment about which she was writing.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5958667994050720599">A wonderful story, beautifully told. Kimberley Freeman is an amazing author. Wildflower Hill is two love stories, one set in the present day, the other in the 1930's. A white woman and an aboriginal man in the 1930's could only cause a scandal - what were they to do when their hearts beat as one? The modern day story of a famous ballerina provides a different twist. Highly recommended.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_741703131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/741703131" />
    <a title="Peggy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3941502-peggy"><img alt="Peggy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600198942p2/3941502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/741703131?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peggy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peggy" href="/user/show/3941502-peggy">Peggy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3941502-peggy?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer741703131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12872162223591564329">A fast-paced, easy-to-read, never boring book. I really enjoyed it! It took me a few chapters to really get into the story, but once it did, it didn't let me go. I'm talking about Beattie's story here, which interested me much more than Emma's. All those things Beattie went through in her life, poor her. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I was so sad when Charlie died! Although Beattie really annoyed me at that point (and only that point): what is it with those white women who have good romantic or other relation</span></span>
  <span id="freeText12872162223591564329" style="display:none">A fast-paced, easy-to-read, never boring book. I really enjoyed it! It took me a few chapters to really get into the story, but once it did, it didn't let me go. I'm talking about Beattie's story here, which interested me much more than Emma's. All those things Beattie went through in her life, poor her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I was so sad when Charlie died! Although Beattie really annoyed me at that point (and only that point): what is it with those white women who have good romantic or other relationships with black people, and just can't understand that it's not that easy, they should be careful, and it's always the black people who will be blamed for everything, and that something will be made up to blame them for if there's nothing real. In a way I blame Beattie for Charlie's death: if she had listened to him more and not declared their love in front of everyone... On the other hand, I can imagine how frustrating it must be to be surrounded by such narrow-minded and prejudiced people, that at some point you just forget about it all.<br />I was also saddened by the fact that she never ever saw Lucy again, had hardly any contact with her, except for that one harsh letter from her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I would have liked to read a bit more about Beattie, before the story jumped to 1965 and the last 20 years or so were sort of skimmed over. It might have been nice to have a more elaborate story about her way to success. <br /><br />Emma, on the other hand, I did not care for. When a chapter finished and the story jumped back to Emma I felt some frustration, I really wanted to read more about Beattie! Besides Beattie's story being much more interesting, I also did not like Emma at all. So arrogant and selfish, and I can't believe she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ jumped on that plane as soon as her cheating boyfriend called and got back to him without questions, not caring AT ALL about all the people in Tasmania, especially Mina and Patrick. I can't really deal with those women who seem to have no self-respect at all and depend completely on their boyfriends. I'm glad she changed her mind in the end, but I still don't like her and think Patrick deserves much better.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I would have liked a bit more story in the epilogue too. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I suspect Lucy was happy to receive the letter, but I'd like to know for sure! To know a bit more about what happened after that, but also how Lucy felt about her mom in all those years she didn't see her. Did she continue to feel the same as she felt in her letter for all those 60-70 years?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="12872162223591564329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_134538960" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134538960" />
    <a title="Kate Forsyth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3237560-kate-forsyth"><img alt="Kate Forsyth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329268435p2/3237560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134538960?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Forsyth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Forsyth" href="/user/show/3237560-kate-forsyth">Kate Forsyth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780733623752" href="/book/show/9322690-wildflower-hill">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3237560-kate-forsyth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3237560-kate-forsyth?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3237560-kate-forsyth?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134538960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10772385755461796903">A compelling and poignant family saga that parallels the story of Beattie Blaxland, a Scottish girl who emigrates to Australia in 1929, with the story of her granddaughter, Emma Blaxland-Hunter. Linking the generations is the old house, Wildflower Hill, in Tasmania. A love story, and a story about making the best of what life throws at you, this is a book where the pages just seem to turn themselves. I’d really recommend this to anyone who loves a heart-warming tale.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3141353526347416793">I decided to read this book based on goodreads and amazon recommendations, I think because I had really liked Kate Morton's The Forgotten Garden.   <span id="freeText3141353526347416793" style="display:none">I decided to read this book based on goodreads and amazon recommendations, I think because I had really liked Kate Morton's The Forgotten Garden. When it arrived I saw Morton had even written a blurb for the front cover so I was all excited for it. But then I read it and was really really disappointed. I felt like Morton's blurb should have read: Nice try but not as good as my book. The plot of this book is very similar to The Forgotten Garden (generations of women, family secrets, inheritances, Australia) but Freeman is not as good at portraying the characters and they all felt like stereotypes to me, especially the ballerina grandaughter. The plot of this book is also so painfully predictable that I almost laughed when every plot "twist" happened. Oh and it's over 500 pages long so it just goes on and on and you know exactly what is going to happen in the end. So learn from my mistakes, don't read this book, read The Forgotten Garden instead!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MomToKippy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MomToKippy" href="/user/show/4631503-momtokippy">MomToKippy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4631503-momtokippy?shelf=historical-fiction-romance">historical-fiction-romance</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer784940664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9289947844328758261">I would give this 3.5 stars overall but 4 for Beattie's story. This is a dual time period story where the historical portion is much more endearing than the contemporary story. In fact, I felt that the modern story really contributed very little to the overall impact of the heart wrenching saga of Beattie's life and struggles. In this case, the author did not really use it to its best advantage in discovering the past. It seemed to be just part of the popular formula for dual time period fiction</span>
  <span id="freeText9289947844328758261" style="display:none">I would give this 3.5 stars overall but 4 for Beattie's story. This is a dual time period story where the historical portion is much more endearing than the contemporary story. In fact, I felt that the modern story really contributed very little to the overall impact of the heart wrenching saga of Beattie's life and struggles. In this case, the author did not really use it to its best advantage in discovering the past. It seemed to be just part of the popular formula for dual time period fiction. It would be a better book if the 1929 story were more detailed and the contemporary story removed entirely. The period switches felt disjointed to me. Possibly because of this it took me about 150 pages to get really interested in the story.<br /><br />Anyway, Beattie's story was beautiful and tragic. The advice that helps motivates her in several dire situations was memorable. "There are 2 kinds of women, those who do things and those who have things done to them." I do wish she had not had so many things "done to her." It was a bit sad and some she was not able to overcome. The story lines with her daughter and Charlie were agonizing. I would prefer to have some happier resolutions to the story but that's just me.<br /><br />The Tasmania setting was fascinating and the characters in that time period were vividly drawn. One easily identified with their love, hate and quirkiness. I could see that portion of the story would make quite a good movie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9289947844328758261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13362454474157978054">Historical family saga spanning over 80 years that intertwines the life a a young woman and her grandmother. <br/><br/>This was a terrific read and I enjoyed it immensely.   <span id="freeText13362454474157978054" style="display:none">Historical family saga spanning over 80 years that intertwines the life a a young woman and her grandmother. <br /><br />This was a terrific read and I enjoyed it immensely. The story grabbed me from the first page to the very last and I particularly liked how the author wove the two stories together. I often struggle with dual timelines. Just when I am getting into the flow of one character's story, I am catapulted into the next. However, the author's movement from one story to the next was seamless.<br /><br />Though, I actually found myself disappointed in both women, it didn't take away from my enjoyment of the book which in itself is a testimony of good writing. I think this would be a terrific selection for a Ladies Book Group. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ For me, Beattie (grandmother) didn't seem to grow. In the beginning, I could accept her poor decisions as just youthful mistakes. But as the story progressed, I found she was more a victim of her poor choices rather than the bitter challenges life threw her way. On the other hand, Emma (granddaughter) did grow, but unfortunately her story didn't grab me as much. I also didn't see that Beattie's story influenced the granddaughter's final decisions.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_151716052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151716052" />
    <a title="Karen Brooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2382210-karen-brooks"><img alt="Karen Brooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450143415p2/2382210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151716052?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Brooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Brooks" href="/user/show/2382210-karen-brooks">Karen Brooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780733623752" href="/book/show/9322690-wildflower-hill">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151716052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16993975586976903221">Being a huge fan of Kim Wilkins work, it was with great curiosity and excitement that I picked up this book, written under her non de plume, Kimberely Freeman, and marking another genre for this incredibly talented writer. I already know what a masterful storyteller Wilkins is and, writing as Freemen, she doesn't disappoint. This tale of two women from the same family, told across two different time periods and in two hemispheres is compelling, tragic, thrilling and uplifting. Commencing in 1995</span>
  <span id="freeText16993975586976903221" style="display:none">Being a huge fan of Kim Wilkins work, it was with great curiosity and excitement that I picked up this book, written under her non de plume, Kimberely Freeman, and marking another genre for this incredibly talented writer. I already know what a masterful storyteller Wilkins is and, writing as Freemen, she doesn't disappoint. This tale of two women from the same family, told across two different time periods and in two hemispheres is compelling, tragic, thrilling and uplifting. Commencing in 1995 and swiftly moving back in time to 1930s Scotland, before shifting to Australia, it tells of one woman's search for love, place and above all, self and against the backdrop of the Depression and looming war. Beattie Blaxland starts as a woman moulded by her upbringing and the prejudices of class, sex and race. However, instead of being a woman who 'things are done to' she becomes a woman 'who does things' and, in doing so, forges a remarkable path into the future - and not only her own.<br /><br />That decades later, her supremely talented granddaughter, prima ballerina Emma, benefits from her grandmother's trailblazing only to have her comfortable world fall apart, is at first heart-breaking. But Emma is imbued with the Blaxland spirit and, the more she learns, through an unexpected legacy, about her grandmother's past, the more she learns about herself.<br /><br />This book gallops along, taking the reader by the hand and heart, plunging you into great joy and sorrow, tragedy and triumph. I read it in one sitting (well, it was broken by a general anesthetic - really!), but I couldn't put it down and longed to find out what happened. It's a powerful and moving tale about longing, loss, family, place, community and the various forces that shape the self within these and how, if we look deep enough, we can find the strength to endure what at first seems unendurable.<br /><br />Simply a beautiful story that I cannot recommend highly enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16993975586976903221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1731971831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1731971831" />
    <a title="Liza Fireman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28266634-liza-fireman"><img alt="Liza Fireman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391265546p2/28266634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1731971831?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liza Fireman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liza Fireman" href="/user/show/28266634-liza-fireman">Liza Fireman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28266634-liza-fireman?shelf=4000-books">4000-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28266634-liza-fireman?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28266634-liza-fireman?shelf=read-audible">read-audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28266634-liza-fireman?shelf=read-from-shelf">read-from-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1731971831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4541234162339460033">This book is in between being a well written chick-lit, and a great novel. It is an easy read, interesting and fun. It goes between past and present, but in a wonderful way. Beattie's story is much more interesting than Emma's story, but they work well together.<br/><br/>It also has a very feministic message, which is always a great thing: <i> There are two types of women in the world, Beattie, those who do things and those who have things done to them. Try to be the first type.” </i> It is about strength and ha</span>
  <span id="freeText4541234162339460033" style="display:none">This book is in between being a well written chick-lit, and a great novel. It is an easy read, interesting and fun. It goes between past and present, but in a wonderful way. Beattie's story is much more interesting than Emma's story, but they work well together.<br /><br />It also has a very feministic message, which is always a great thing: <i> There are two types of women in the world, Beattie, those who do things and those who have things done to them. Try to be the first type.” </i> It is about strength and hard work, it is about taking your fate in your own hands, it's about being independent.<br /><br />I also liked this quote about books: <i>“Once you’ve read a book, you and it belong to each other for life. Did you not know that?”<br />“Even the pulpy ones?”<br />“Even the pulpy ones.”</i><br /><br />There are questions of love, strength and even race and prejudice in the book. And there are the question of age. What do we know about our parents or grandparents lives? We almost never think about their loves, struggles, enjoyable moments, since they have a role in our lives, and we know them mostly through a one dimensional view of this role. But there's always more: <i>So did Grandma have more than one lover? Was the little girl in the photo her daughter? Who was the man who came for the little red-haired child? I wanted to believe, like Mum, that Granddad was the first. The only.<br />But the worst mistake we can make about old people is to forget they were young once.</i><br /><br />Beattie is an amazing character. An outstanding woman with a great story. Lovely writing and good plot (except some Emma parts, but she's not the main point). 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4541234162339460033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_205918094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205918094" />
    <a title="Britni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/389139-britni"><img alt="Britni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598115687p2/389139.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205918094?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Britni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Britni" href="/user/show/389139-britni">Britni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205918094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14447437930281325257">According to Cora, there are two types of people in the world - those who do things and those who have things done to them.<br/><br/>Emma has always been a woman who does things, who fought her way to the coveted spot of a prima ballerina in a London ballet company. Until one dark night her career as a ballerina is cut short and her life takes on a different course, one that takes her to the home of her recently deceased grandmother, Beattie, in Tasmania. While clearing out Beattie's home, Emma finds clue</span>
  <span id="freeText14447437930281325257" style="display:none">According to Cora, there are two types of people in the world - those who do things and those who have things done to them.<br /><br />Emma has always been a woman who does things, who fought her way to the coveted spot of a prima ballerina in a London ballet company. Until one dark night her career as a ballerina is cut short and her life takes on a different course, one that takes her to the home of her recently deceased grandmother, Beattie, in Tasmania. While clearing out Beattie's home, Emma finds clues to the story of Beattie's life that know one knew other than Beattie herself. A small red-haired child, a love letter that couldn't have been written to Emma's grandpa, and rumors of a scandalous poker game.<br /><br />Wildflower Hill is written from the perspective of these two women - Emma and Beattie - as they tell their stories seventy years apart. The book alternates between their stories and help you piece together the puzzle and the significance of Wildflower Hill in both women's lives.<br /><br />After I picked this book up, I couldn't put it down and finished it in 48 hours. Even with all of her flaws, I loved Beattie's character and had to know what happened to her and how her story played out. The book is full of heart-breaking twists that I hated but quickly saw were essential to the story. This is the first book I've read by Kimberly Freeman. She made her characters come to life, the scenery visible through her words, and the story was believable and made me want to read more. 5 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14447437930281325257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_205268156" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205268156" />
    <a title="Lindsey (Bring My Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4382458-lindsey-bring-my-books"><img alt="Lindsey (Bring My Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603997081p2/4382458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205268156?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey (Bring My Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey (Bring My Books)" href="/user/show/4382458-lindsey-bring-my-books">Lindsey (Bring My Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4382458-lindsey-bring-my-books?shelf=dual-timeline">dual-timeline</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205268156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9137554758203828379">It's been quite some time since a book kept me up until 2am! (One more chapter, just one more chapter, okay, just until this page...okay, just until I know what happens with this...okay, just one more chapter...-I'm sure we've all been there!) <br/><br/>Such a wonderfully vivid portrayal of these two women's lives. It's so interesting to read a novel with intertwining lives decades apart that *doesn't* have a big reveal at the end (where the present-day character comes to understand everything that occure</span>
  <span id="freeText9137554758203828379" style="display:none">It's been quite some time since a book kept me up until 2am! (One more chapter, just one more chapter, okay, just until this page...okay, just until I know what happens with this...okay, just one more chapter...-I'm sure we've all been there!) <br /><br />Such a wonderfully vivid portrayal of these two women's lives. It's so interesting to read a novel with intertwining lives decades apart that *doesn't* have a big reveal at the end (where the present-day character comes to understand everything that occured in the past character's life.) The present-day character, Emma, was given a much better idea of who her grandmother Beattie was, while still not knowing the full gravity of what her grandmother endured. I think it created so much depth for me as a reader. I felt inextricably linked to each of the characaters, especially Beattie (the woman from the past). It was as though I was living her life alongside her, feeling each loss and joy just as she would. If an author can create that kind of a relationship between her characters and her reader, there really isn't anything more that I could ask of her. Brilliant book. Hope for more from Ms. Freeman along these lines!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9137554758203828379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3198574141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12454687834156806700">This dual timeline novel had some real creative strengths. The Australian setting was interesting and different, and I loved the professions of the two main characters -- one was a ballet dancer, and the other was a clothing designer. And both of them, in different time periods, occupied a sheep ranch in Tasmania. Both women had several love affairs -- but these seemed rather insipid compared to the truly passionate illicit affair that took place in the earlier storyline, in 1939. Although both </span>
  <span id="freeText12454687834156806700" style="display:none">This dual timeline novel had some real creative strengths. The Australian setting was interesting and different, and I loved the professions of the two main characters -- one was a ballet dancer, and the other was a clothing designer. And both of them, in different time periods, occupied a sheep ranch in Tasmania. Both women had several love affairs -- but these seemed rather insipid compared to the truly passionate illicit affair that took place in the earlier storyline, in 1939. Although both stories came to a satisfactory conclusion, my only caveat is that the woman who lived in the earlier time period suffered two great tragedies, neither of which was resolved during her lifetime, and that made me feel very sad.</span>

<div id="review_1678293133" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Denise Deen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23291335-denise-deen"><img alt="Denise Deen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581126170p2/23291335.jpg" /></a>

      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1678293133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7966929274887242525">4.5 stars.......This is a gorgeous story of family and secrets with the backdrop of beautiful, isolated rural Australia in the 1930's and current time. Parallel stories of a grandmother and granddaughter both of which find themselves, love and their life's path in the magic of a sheep farm on Wildflower Hill. I thoroughly enjoyed both story lines but Beattie (grandmother) really touched my heart with her courage, hard work and compassion. This is a sweeping, romantic and compelling read.</span>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=australia">australia</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223719452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3758618833301066133">This is a story that will grab you, suck you with force straight into the pages, and leave you feeling bereft when you turn the last page.<br/><br/><br/>You have a woman who after stealing another woman's husband, pays for it for the rest of her life. Another woman steals another's child and she pays for that the rest of her life... People love who they want to love and shun society's stupid rules...and pay with their lives. You have a heroine...who...though she irritated the crap out of me at times, is incred</span>
  <span id="freeText3758618833301066133" style="display:none">This is a story that will grab you, suck you with force straight into the pages, and leave you feeling bereft when you turn the last page.<br /><br /><br />You have a woman who after stealing another woman's husband, pays for it for the rest of her life. Another woman steals another's child and she pays for that the rest of her life... People love who they want to love and shun society's stupid rules...and pay with their lives. You have a heroine...who...though she irritated the crap out of me at times, is incredibly tough. I mean, she risks everything for those she loves, even if it means losing them.<br /><br />And that's just the historical bits. The contemporary woman is a dancer whose career has come to a sudden halt and she must realize just what is important in life...that perhaps it's time to think of others and she realizes how much she's been missing out whilst she's been wrapped up in herself and her dancing career.<br /><br />I preferred the historical story even though it was full of heartache and frustration. Beattie...in the 1930s...the way she packs up her stuff and walks in the rain to escape a loser "husband"...the way she stood up to the religious lady she sought refuge with...the way she made an incredibly daring bet with a landowner. "If I win, I get the land and the house. If you win, you get my body.." (not a direct quote)<br /><br />I mean, just wow. What guts. And how she came to rule a wool fashion empire...<br /><br />Her love affair...so passionate and so sad, yet, I wasn't surprised by the outcome. So much bigotry and hate back then.<br /><br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://wwwbookbabe.blogspot.com/2013/09/wildflower-hill-by-kimberley-freeman.html#.UiLsuDaThK0">http://wwwbookbabe.blogspot.com/2013/...</a></span>

<div id="review_153135992" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153135992" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5043303-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298767179p2/5043303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153135992?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/5043303-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780733623752" href="/book/show/9322690-wildflower-hill">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153135992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6143472721638072743">This book is by Brisbane author Kim Wilkins, who normally writes fantasy fiction. Under the guise of Kimberley Freeman she has written this unputdownable story of two women, separated in time. Beattie Blaxland is a 19 year old girl in 1920's Glasgow when she discovers she is pregnant to her married lover. All her hopes and dreams are shattered, and she ends up emigrating to Tasmania where she endures many hardships. Beattie's granddaughter Emma is a world famous ballerina, living in modern day L</span>
  <span id="freeText6143472721638072743" style="display:none">This book is by Brisbane author Kim Wilkins, who normally writes fantasy fiction. Under the guise of Kimberley Freeman she has written this unputdownable story of two women, separated in time. Beattie Blaxland is a 19 year old girl in 1920's Glasgow when she discovers she is pregnant to her married lover. All her hopes and dreams are shattered, and she ends up emigrating to Tasmania where she endures many hardships. Beattie's granddaughter Emma is a world famous ballerina, living in modern day London, when a nasty injury and a break up with her partner force her back to Australia. There she discovers she has inherited 'Wildflower Hill', Beattie's Tasmanian homestead, and despite her misgivings she goes there, to pack up her grandmother's things and put the house on the market. <br />This story is masterfully told, and beautifully crafted. The characters are rich and engaging, and I especially love that everyone is very three dimensional. Even Henry, the married lover of Beattie, who becomes a drunk and a gambler has his good points (he loves his daughter unconditionally, he admits to his faults as a partner and father, he tries to share Lucy equally with Beattie, he doesn't mind if people are black, etc). <br />I couldn't put this book down, and was so sad when it ended. This is an outstanding book in a genre where there are many mediocre books, and I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6143472721638072743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_208753008" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208753008" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3860512-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318554080p2/3860512.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208753008?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/3860512-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208753008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15061358210749721403">I haven't felt such a full range of emotions from a novel in a long time. This dual-narrative novel was exciting, heartbreaking, romantic, frustrating and mysterious, and kept me, for the most part, interested in both the characters, their lives and how resolution would be found. I enjoyed Emma's story line, but my heart was with Beattie and all that she went through as life threw more ups and downs than any average person is given. I felt for her the most, and wanted her story to have turned ou</span>
  <span id="freeText15061358210749721403" style="display:none">I haven't felt such a full range of emotions from a novel in a long time. This dual-narrative novel was exciting, heartbreaking, romantic, frustrating and mysterious, and kept me, for the most part, interested in both the characters, their lives and how resolution would be found. I enjoyed Emma's story line, but my heart was with Beattie and all that she went through as life threw more ups and downs than any average person is given. I felt for her the most, and wanted her story to have turned out differently. Mostly I wish that she had been afforded the opportunity to be with the love of her life, and not have him taken in such a brutal, hateful way. <br />I am glad that Emma found her way to real life after the end of her dancing career. Sometimes we have to take a step back at our life to see that what we think gives us happiness, is not real but a cover for emptiness that we would feel if life weren't so busy. She is given the chance to slow down, and start fresh. <br />I liked the two time periods, but wished a bit more for a description of Tasmania and Australia. It might have made me feel as though I had really been there. I had to remind myself that this wasn't an American novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15061358210749721403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4122537243766533712">The book switches back between present time and the past. Emma is a famous ballerina from Australia, living in London. She falls severely injuring her knee and is told her ballerina career is over. Her boyfriend breaks off their relationship just before her devastating injury and she decides to travel back to Australia. Her grandmother, Beattie died sometime previously and when Emma arrives home, she discovers she has inherited her grandmother's abandoned sheep farm in Tasmania. Emma travels to </span>
  <span id="freeText4122537243766533712" style="display:none">The book switches back between present time and the past. Emma is a famous ballerina from Australia, living in London. She falls severely injuring her knee and is told her ballerina career is over. Her boyfriend breaks off their relationship just before her devastating injury and she decides to travel back to Australia. Her grandmother, Beattie died sometime previously and when Emma arrives home, she discovers she has inherited her grandmother's abandoned sheep farm in Tasmania. Emma travels to Tasmania to check out the property, ready it for sale and have some time to rethink her life. The book switches back and forth between present time and back to when Beattie as a young woman left England, travelled to Tasmania; her challenges, her perserverance in trying to make a life for herself during the late 1930's and early 1940's. Beattie became a very successful businesswoman but her challenges in life and the secrets she kept throughout her life begin to surface as Emma goes through her boxes stored in the old farmstead. Emma meets people in the local area and starts building roots in the community discovering what is truly important in life. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer374518645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11322202585940581212">I really wanted to like this book. I thought the plot line about a poor Scottish unwed single mother, Beattie, coming to Australia and becoming a successful sheep farmer in the 1930s had so much potential, particularly since much of her story looked as if it would be told through her granddaughter, Emma. But alas, while the story itself was entertaining, the characters were so flat and one dimensional it was hard to connect with them, so I became rather apathetic as events unfolded. The ending w</span>
  <span id="freeText11322202585940581212" style="display:none">I really wanted to like this book. I thought the plot line about a poor Scottish unwed single mother, Beattie, coming to Australia and becoming a successful sheep farmer in the 1930s had so much potential, particularly since much of her story looked as if it would be told through her granddaughter, Emma. But alas, while the story itself was entertaining, the characters were so flat and one dimensional it was hard to connect with them, so I became rather apathetic as events unfolded. The ending was so unfulfilling, and I probably would have screamed out loud if I had cared more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11322202585940581212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1514221496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1115484934285481462">I enjoyed the mystery surrounding this story and how the grandmother's story was discovered by her granddaughter while also being told by herself in the past. Emma, the granddaughter was a ballerina so she was quite snobby often and this was irritating but she became a real person in the end. I wonder what reaction Lucy had to her letter she received towards the end of the book. We'll never know. I would have felt guilty if I were her. Good story.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ti1EVdBr6ML+1wLw+AcsSb2prldgxonjGzVrM2wWxCtOAjxLEkZ/KKP7I5akfo30LZtMIeOs8roo2jJM8u4qEA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C4wU/Zf9P8m2xdF+cAnc8aGsTVaLcMfk7DzKWxl6+AYLo2zjVdCoI+vp8BgscH1MMZ6vIAgavL3f05Mkh4IWPQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer12141573965679026936">Pen name of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/344352.Kim_Wilkins' title='Kim Wilkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kim Wilkins</a>.<br/><br/><br/>Kimberley was born in London and her family moved back to Australia when she was three years old. She grew up in Queensland where she currently lives.<br/><br/>Kimberley has written for as long as she can remember and she is proud to write in many genres. She is an award-winning writer in children’s, historical and speculative fiction under her birth name Kim Wilkins. She adopted the</span>
  <span id="freeText12141573965679026936" style="display:none">Pen name of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/344352.Kim_Wilkins" title="Kim Wilkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Kim Wilkins</a>.<br /><br /><br />Kimberley was born in London and her family moved back to Australia when she was three years old. She grew up in Queensland where she currently lives.<br /><br />Kimberley has written for as long as she can remember and she is proud to write in many genres. She is an award-winning writer in children’s, historical and speculative fiction under her birth name Kim Wilkins. She adopted the pen name Kimberley Freeman for her commercial women’s fiction novels Duet and Gold Dust to honour her maternal grandmother and to try and capture the spirit of the page-turning novels she has always loved to read. Kim has an Honours degree, a Masters degree and a PhD from The University of Queensland where she is also a lecturer. She lives in Brisbane with her young family.<br /></span>
